    <script type="text/javascript">
        var supportWindowsHistory = !!(window.history && window.history.pushState);
        // In downgraded browsers we need to use the hash in order to reach the angular routes
        if (!supportWindowsHistory) {
            if (window.location.hash.charAt(1) !== "!") {
                var baseHref = document.getElementsByTagName('base')[0].href;
                var hashRoute = location.href.replace(baseHref, "").replace(location.hash, "");
                window.location.replace(window.location.pathname + '#!' + hashRoute + window.location.search + window.location.hash);
            }
        }
    </script>

builds that were released after SQL Server 2005 Service Pack 4 was released</td>\n\t\t\t</tr>\n\t\t</tbody>\n\t</table>\n\t</div>\n\t</li>\n</ul>\n<a class=\"bookmark\" id=\"howtodetermine\"></a>\n\n<div class=\"faq-section\" faq-section=\"\">\n<div class=\"faq-panel\">\n<div class=\"faq-panel-heading\" faq-panel-heading=\"\"><span class=\"link-expand-image\"><span class=\"faq-chevron win-icon win-icon-ChevronUpSmall\"></span></span><span class=\"bold btn-link link-expand-text\"><span class=\"bold btn-link\">How to determine which version and edition of SQL Server Database Engine is running</span></span></div>\n\n<div class=\"faq-panel-body\" faq-panel-body=\"\">\n<div class=\"kb-collapsible kb-collapsible-collapsed\">To determine the version of SQL Server, you can use any of the following methods.<br>\n<br>\n<strong>Method 1:</strong> Connect to the server by using Object Explorer in SQL Server Management Studio. After Object Explorer is connected, it will show the version information in parentheses, together with the user name that is used to connect to the specific instance of SQL Server.<br>\n<br>\n<strong>Method 2:</strong> Look at the first few lines of the Errorlog file for that instance. By default, the error log is located at Program Files\\Microsoft SQL Server\\MSSQL.<span class=\"sbody-italic\">n</span>\\MSSQL\\LOG\\ERRORLOG and ERRORLOG.<span class=\"sbody-italic\">n</span> files. The entries may resemble the following:<br>\n&nbsp;\n<pre class=\"sbody-pre\">\n\n2011-03-27 22:31:33.50 Server      Microsoft SQL Server 2008 (SP1) - \n10.0.2531.0 (X64)\n\n                March 29 2009 10:11:52\n\n                Copyright (c) 1988-2008 Microsoft Corporation\n\nExpress Edition (64-bit)\non Windows NT 6.1 &lt;X64&gt; (Build 7600: ) </pre>\n<br>\nThis entry provides all the necessary information about the product, such as version, product level, 64-bit versus 32-bit, the edition of SQL Server, and the OS version on which SQL Server is running.<br>\n<br>\n<strong>Note</strong> The output of this query has been enhanced to show additional information, as documented in the blog post article, <a href=\"http://blogs.msdn.com/b/psssql/archive/2015/07/20/what-build-of-sql-server-are-you-running.aspx\" id=\"kb-link-38\" target=\"_self\">What build of SQL Server are you using?</a>, for the following versions:<br>\n&nbsp;\n<ul class=\"sbody-free_list\">\n\t<li>SQL Server 2014 RTM CU10 and later versions</li>\n\t<li>SQL Server 2014 Service Pack 1 CU3 and later versions</li>\n\t<li>SQL Server 2012 Service Pack 2 CU7 and later versions</li>\n</ul>\n<br>\n<strong>Method 3:</strong> Connect to the instance of SQL Server, and then run the following query:\n\n<div class=\"indent\"><span class=\"text-base\"></span>\n\n<pre class=\"sbody-pre\">\n\nSelect @@version </pre>\n</div>\nAn example of the output of this query is the following:\n\n<pre class=\"sbody-pre\">\n\nMicrosoft SQL Server 2008 (SP1) - \n10.0.2531.0 (X64)\n  March 29 2009 10:11:52 Copyright (c) 1988-2008 Microsoft Corporation\nExpress Edition (64-bit)\n  on Windows NT 6.1 &lt;X64&gt; (Build 7600: ) </pre>\n<br>\n<br>\n<strong>Note</strong> The output of this query has been enhanced to show additional information. This is documented in the blog post article, <a href=\"http://blogs.msdn.com/b/psssql/archive/2015/07/20/what-build-of-sql-server-are-you-running.aspx\" id=\"kb-link-39\" target=\"_self\">What build of SQL Server are you using?</a>, for the following versions:<br>\n&nbsp;\n<ul class=\"sbody-free_list\">\n\t<li>SQL Server 2014 RTM CU10 and later versions</li>\n\t<li>SQL Server 2014 Service Pack 1 CU3 and later versions</li>\n\t<li>SQL Server 2012 Service Pack 2 CU7 and later versions<br>\n\t<br>\n\t<img alt=\"Example of changed output \" class=\"graphic\" src=\"/Library/Images/3118884.jpg\" title=\"Example of changed output \"></li>\n</ul>\n<br>\n<strong>Method 4:</strong> Connect to the instance of SQL Server, and then run the following query in SQL Server Management Studio (SSMS):\n\n<div class=\"indent\">\n<pre class=\"sbody-pre\">\n\nSELECT SERVERPROPERTY(&#39;productversion&#39;), SERVERPROPERTY (&#39;productlevel&#39;),\n\nSERVERPROPERTY (&#39;edition&#39;) </pre>\n</div>\n<strong>Note</strong> This query works for any instance of SQL Server 2000 or a later version.<br>\n<br>\nThe following results are returned:<br>\n&nbsp;\n<ul class=\"sbody-free_list\">\n\t<li>The product version (for example, 10.0.1600.22)</li>\n\t<li>The product level (for example, RTM)</li>\n\t<li>The edition (for example, Enterprise)</li>\n</ul>\n<br>\nFor example, the results resemble the following.<br>\n&nbsp;\n<div class=\"table-responsive\">\n<table class=\"table\">\n\t<tbody>\n\t\t<tr class=\"sbody-tr\">\n\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\"><span class=\"text-base\">10.0.1600.22</span></td>\n\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\">RTM</td>\n\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\"><span class=\"text-base\">Enterprise Edition</span></td>\n\t\t</tr>\n\t</tbody>\n</table>\n</div>\n<span class=\"text-base\"></span><br>\n<strong>Notes</strong><br>\n&nbsp;\n<ul class=\"sbody-free_list\">\n\t<li>The <span class=\"text-base\">SERVERPROPERTY </span>function returns individual properties that relate to the version information, although the <span class=\"text-base\">@@VERSION</span>function combines the output into one string. If your application requires individual property strings, you can use the <span class=\"text-base\">SERVERPROPERTY </span>function to return them instead of parsing the <span class=\"text-base\">@@VERSION</span>results.</li>\n\t<li>This method also works for SQL Azure Database instances. For additional information refer to the following topic in SQL Server Books Online <a href=\"https://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/library/ms174396.aspx\" id=\"kb-link-40\" target=\"_self\">SERVERPROPERTY (Transact-SQL)</a>.</li>\n\t<li>Starting with <a href=\"/en-us/help/3094220\" id=\"kb-link-41\" target=\"_self\">SQL Server 2014 RTM Cumulative Update 10</a> and <a href=\"/en-us/help/3094221\" id=\"kb-link-42\" target=\"_self\">SQL Server 2014 Service Pack 1 Cumulative Update 3</a>, additional properties have been added to ServerProperty statement as noted in the following table.<br>\n\t&nbsp;\n\t<div class=\"table-responsive\">\n\t<table class=\"table\">\n\t\t<tbody>\n\t\t\t<tr class=\"sbody-tr\">\n\t\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\"><span class=\"text-base\">ProductBuildType </span></td>\n\t\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\">Type of build of the current build.<br>\n\t\t\t\t<br>\n\t\t\t\tReturns one of the following:<br>\n\t\t\t\t&nbsp;\n\t\t\t\t<ul class=\"sbody-free_list\">\n\t\t\t\t\t<li>OD = OD released to the web for a particular customer</li>\n\t\t\t\t\t<li>GDR = GDR released through windows update</li>\n\t\t\t\t\t<li>NULL = Not applicable</li>\n\t\t\t\t</ul>\n\t\t\t\t</td>\n\t\t\t</tr>\n\t\t\t<tr class=\"sbody-tr\">\n\t\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\"><span class=\"text-base\">ProductLevel</span></td>\n\t\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\">Level of the version of the instance of SQL Server.<br>\n\t\t\t\t<br>\n\t\t\t\tReturns one of the following:<br>\n\t\t\t\t&nbsp;\n\t\t\t\t<ul class=\"sbody-free_list\">\n\t\t\t\t\t<li>&#39;RTM&#39; = Original release version</li>\n\t\t\t\t\t<li>&#39;SP<span class=\"sbody-italic\">n</span>&#39; = Service pack version</li>\n\t\t\t\t\t<li>&#39;CTP<span class=\"sbody-italic\">n</span>&#39;, = Community Technology Preview version</li>\n\t\t\t\t</ul>\n\t\t\t\t&hellip;</td>\n\t\t\t</tr>\n\t\t\t<tr class=\"sbody-tr\">\n\t\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\"><span class=\"text-base\">ProductUpdateLevel</span></td>\n\t\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\">Update level of the current build.<br>\n\t\t\t\t<br>\n\t\t\t\tReturns one of the following:<br>\n\t\t\t\t&nbsp;\n\t\t\t\t<ul class=\"sbody-free_list\">\n\t\t\t\t\t<li>CU<span class=\"sbody-italic\">n</span> = Cumulative Update</li>\n\t\t\t\t\t<li>NULL = Not applicable</li>\n\t\t\t\t</ul>\n\t\t\t\t</td>\n\t\t\t</tr>\n\t\t\t<tr class=\"sbody-tr\">\n\t\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\"><span class=\"text-base\">ProductUpdateReference</span></td>\n\t\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\">KB article for that release</td>\n\t\t\t</tr>\n\t\t\t<tr class=\"sbody-tr\">\n\t\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\"><span class=\"text-base\">ProductBuild</span></td>\n\t\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\">The build number</td>\n\t\t\t</tr>\n\t\t\t<tr class=\"sbody-tr\">\n\t\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\"><span class=\"text-base\">ProductMajorVersion</span></td>\n\t\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\">The major version</td>\n\t\t\t</tr>\n\t\t\t<tr class=\"sbody-tr\">\n\t\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\"><span class=\"text-base\">ProductMinorVersion</span></td>\n\t\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\">The minor version</td>\n\t\t\t</tr>\n\t\t\t<tr class=\"sbody-tr\">\n\t\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\"><span class=\"text-base\">InstanceDefaultDataPath</span></td>\n\t\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\">This is default location where the data files for any database in this instance will be created. This value is specified in the Data Directories tab or /SQLUSERDBDIR parameter during setup.</td>\n\t\t\t</tr>\n\t\t\t<tr class=\"sbody-tr\">\n\t\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\"><span class=\"text-base\">InstanceDefaultLogPath</span></td>\n\t\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\">This is default location where the log files for any database in this instance will be created. This value is specified in the Data Directories tab or /SQLUSERDBLOGDIR parameter during setup.</td>\n\t\t\t</tr>\n\t\t</tbody>\n\t</table>\n\t</div>\n\tExample output:\n\n\t<div class=\"sbody-code\">\n\t<pre>\n\n<code>SELECT\nSERVERPROPERTY(&#39;ProductLevel&#39;) AS ProductLevel,\nSERVERPROPERTY(&#39;ProductUpdateLevel&#39;) AS ProductUpdateLevel,\nSERVERPROPERTY(&#39;ProductBuildType&#39;) AS ProductBuildType,\nSERVERPROPERTY(&#39;ProductUpdateReference&#39;) AS ProductUpdateReference,\nSERVERPROPERTY(&#39;ProductVersion&#39;) AS ProductVersion,\nSERVERPROPERTY(&#39;ProductMajorVersion&#39;) AS ProductMajorVersion,\nSERVERPROPERTY(&#39;ProductMinorVersion&#39;) AS ProductMinorVersion,\nSERVERPROPERTY(&#39;ProductBuild&#39;) AS ProductBuild\nGO</code></pre>\n\t</div>\n\n\t<div class=\"table-responsive\">\n\t<table class=\"table\">\n\t\t<tbody>\n\t\t\t<tr class=\"sbody-tr\">\n\t\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\"><span class=\"text-base\">ProductLevel</span></td>\n\t\t\t\t<td class=\"text-base\">ProductMajorVersion</span></td>\n\t\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\"><span class=\"text-base\">ProductMinorVersion</span></td>\n\t\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\"><span class=\"text-base\">ProductBuild</span></td>\n\t\t\t</tr>\n\t\t\t<tr class=\"sbody-tr\">\n\t\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\">SP1</td>\n\t\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\">CU3</td>\n\t\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\">NULL</td>\n\t\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\">KB3094221</td>\n\t\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\">12.0.4425.19</td>\n\t\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\">12</td>\n\t\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\">0</td>\n\t\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\">4425</td>\n\t\t\t</tr>\n\t\t</tbody>\n\t</table>\n\t</div>\n\t</li>\n</ul>\n<a class=\"bookmark\" id=\"method5\"></a><br>\n<strong>Method 5:&nbsp;</strong>Starting in SQL Server 2008, you can also use the Installed SQL Server Features Discovery report. This report can be found by locating the <strong>Tools</strong>&nbsp;page of SQL Server Installation Center. This tool gives information about all the instances of SQL Server that are installed on the system. These include client tools such as SQL Server Management Studio. The only thing to be aware of is that this tool can be run locally only on the system where SQL server is installed. It cannot be used to obtain information about remote servers. For more information, visit the following blog post on the Microsoft Developer Network (MSDN):\n\n<div class=\"indent\"><a href=\"http://blogs.msdn.com/b/petersad/archive/2009/11/13/sql-server-2008-discovery-report.aspx\" id=\"kb-link-43\" target=\"_self\">SQL Server 2008 Discovery Report</a></div>\nA snapshot of a sample report is as follows:<br>\n<br>\n<img alt=\"The screen shot showing a sample report \" class=\"graphic\" src=\"/Library/Images/2560488.png\" title=\"The screen shot showing a sample report \"></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"faq-section\" faq-section=\"\">\n<div class=\"faq-panel\">\n<div class=\"faq-panel-heading\" faq-panel-heading=\"\"><span class=\"link-expand-image\"><span class=\"faq-chevron win-icon win-icon-ChevronUpSmall\"></span></span><span class=\"bold btn-link link-expand-text\"><span class=\"bold btn-link\">How to determine the version of SQL Server Client tools</span></span></div>\n\n<div class=\"faq-panel-body\" faq-panel-body=\"\">\n<div class=\"kb-collapsible kb-collapsible-collapsed\"><span class=\"text-base\">SQL Server Management Studio (SSMS)</span><br>\n<br>\nTo determine which versions of the client tools are installed on your system, start Management Studio, and then click <strong class=\"uiterm\">About</strong> on the <strong class=\"uiterm\">Help</strong> menu. (See the following screen shot.)<br>\n<br>\n<img alt=\"About SSMS \" class=\"graphic\" src=\"/Library/Images/3105303.jpg\" title=\"About SSMS \"><br>\n<br>\n<br>\n<strong>SQL Server Business Intelligence Development Studio (BIDS)</strong><br>\n<br>\nTo check the version of Analysis Services Designer, of Integration Services Designer, or of SQL Server Reporting Services Designer, follow these steps:<br>\n&nbsp;\n<ol class=\"sbody-num_list\">\n\t<li>Under your SQL program group, start SQL Server Business Intelligence Development Studio.</li>\n\t<li>On the <strong class=\"uiterm\">Help</strong> menu, click <strong class=\"uiterm\">About</strong>.</li>\n\t<li>In the <strong class=\"uiterm\">Installed products</strong> list, select the required component, and then notice the version that is given in the <strong class=\"uiterm\">Product details</strong> text box.<br>\n\t(See the following screen shots.)</li>\n</ol>\n<br>\n<strong>SQL Server 2005 / Visual Studio 2005</strong><br>\n&nbsp;\n<p><span asset=\"4098977\" contenteditable=\"false\" props=\"{&quot;size&quot;:&quot;full&quot;}\" unselectable=\"on\">4010566</span><span>&nbsp;</span></p>\n<br>\n<strong>SQL Server 2008 / SQL Server 2008 R2 / Visual Studio 2008</strong><br>\n<br>\n<img alt=\"SQLServer2008&amp;VS2008 \" class=\"graphic\" src=\"/Library/Images/3105305.jpg\" title=\"SQLServer2008&amp;VS2008 \"><br>\n<br>\n<strong>Note</strong> For Business Intelligence features such as Integration Services, Reporting Services, and Analysis Services, you may have to install the latest service packs, cumulative updates, and hotfixes on the client-side computers to obtain the latest fixes while developing SSIS packages, SSRS reports, or Analysis Services cubes.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"faq-section\" faq-section=\"\">\n<div class=\"faq-panel\">\n<div class=\"faq-panel-heading\" btn-link\">SQL Server Reporting Services</span></span></div>\n\n<div class=\"faq-panel-body\" faq-panel-body=\"\">\n<div class=\"kb-collapsible kb-collapsible-collapsed\">To determine the version of SQL Server Reporting Services, refer to the following topic in SQL Server Books Online:\n<div class=\"indent\"><a href=\"http://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/library/bb630446.aspx\" id=\"kb-link-44\" target=\"_self\">How to: Detect Version Information (Reporting Services)</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"faq-section\" faq-section=\"\">\n<div class=\"faq-panel\">\n<div kb-collapsible-collapsed\">To determine the version of SQL Server Integration Services, refer to the following article in the Microsoft Knowledge Base:\n<div class=\"indent\"><a href=\"/default.aspx?scid=kb;en-us;942177\" id=\"kb-link-45\" target=\"_self\">942177</a> How to determine the version of SQL Server Integration Services</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"faq-section\" faq-section=\"\">\n<div class=\"faq-panel\">\n<div class=\"faq-panel-heading\" faq-panel-heading=\"\"><span class=\"link-expand-image\"><span class=\"faq-chevron win-icon win-icon-ChevronUpSmall\"></span></span><span class=\"bold btn-link link-expand-text\"><span class=\"bold btn-link\">SQL Server Analysis Services </span></span></div>\n\n<div class=\"faq-panel-body\" faq-panel-body=\"\">\n<div class=\"kb-collapsible kb-collapsible-collapsed\">To determine the version of SQL Server Analysis Services, use one of the following methods:<br>\n<br>\n<strong>Method 1:</strong> Connect to the server by using <span class=\"text-base\">Object Explorer</span> in SQL Server Management Studio. After Object Explorer is connected, it will show the version information in parentheses, together with the user name that is used to connect to the specific instance of Analysis Services.<br>\n<br>\n<strong>Method 2:</strong> Check the version of the Msmdsrv.exe file in the Analysis Services bin folder. The default locations are shown in the following table.<br>\n&nbsp;\n<div class=\"table-responsive\">\n<table class=\"table\">\n\t<tbody>\n\t\t<tr class=\"sbody-tr\">\n\t\t\t<th class=\"sbody-td\">2008</td>\n\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\">C:\\Program Files\\Microsoft SQL Server\\MSAS10.InstanceName\\OLAP\\bin\\MsMdSrv.exe</td>\n\t\t</tr>\n\t\t<tr class=\"sbody-tr\">\n\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\">2005</td>\n\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\">C:\\Program Files\\Microsoft SQL Server\\MSSQL.n\\OLAP\\Bin\\MsMdSrv.exe</td>\n\t\t</tr>\n\t\t<tr class=\"sbody-tr\">\n\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\">2000</td>\n\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\">C:\\Program Files\\Microsoft Analysis Services\\Bin\\MsMdSrv.exe</td>\n\t\t</tr>\n\t</tbody>\n</table>\n</div>\n<br>\n<strong>Method 3:</strong> Use the registry subkeys that are listed in the following table.<br>\n&nbsp;\n<div class=\"table-responsive\">\n<table class=\"table\">\n\t<tbody>\n\t\t<tr class=\"sbody-tr\">\n\t\t\t<th PatchLevel, Version, Edition</td>\n\t\t</tr>\n\t\t<tr class=\"sbody-tr\">\n\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\">2005</td>\n\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\">HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\\SOFTWARE\\Microsoft\\Microsoft SQL Edition</td>\n\t\t</tr>\n\t\t<tr class=\"sbody-tr\">\n\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\">2000</td>\n\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\">HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\\SOFTWARE\\Microsoft\\OLAP Server\\CurrentVersion Key: CSDVersion<br>\n\t\t\t<br>\n\t\t\tHKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\\SOFTWARE\\Microsoft\\OLAP Server\\Setup Key: PatchLevel</td>\n\t\t</tr>\n\t</tbody>\n</table>\n</div>\n<br>\nFor more information, see the following Microsoft TechNet blog post:\n<div class=\"indent\"><a href=\"http://blogs.technet.com/b/sqlman/archive/2008/03/25/how-to-find-analysis-services-server-version.aspx\" id=\"kb-link-46\" target=\"_self\">How to find Analysis Services Server Version</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"faq-section\" faq-section=\"\">\n<div class=\"faq-panel\">\n<div class=\"faq-panel-heading\" faq-panel-heading=\"\"><span class=\"link-expand-image\"><span class=\"faq-chevron win-icon win-icon-ChevronUpSmall\"></span></span><span class=\"bold btn-link link-expand-text\"><span class=\"bold btn-link\">SQL Server replication</span></span></div>\n\n<div class=\"faq-panel-body\" faq-panel-body=\"\">\n<div class=\"kb-collapsible kb-collapsible-collapsed\">Because replication agents may be installed on several different computers, it is important to check the installed versions on all affected computers.<br>\n<br>\nFor example, the Distribution Agent in Transactional or Peer-to-Peer replication may exist on computers that differ from the publisher instance of SQL Server and may exist on the various subscriber instances of SQL Server in a pull subscription.<br>\n<br>\nIf you use Web Synchronization for Merge Replication or SQL Server 2000 Windows CE Edition replication, the IIS web server may not be the same computer as the computer that is running SQL Server. Therefore, you have replication agent files that are installed on the IIS web server. And you may have to check the version of those .dll files in the IIS virtual directory and update them explicitly to obtain the latest service packs, cumulative updates, and hotfixes for your web agents.<br>\n<br>\nFor more information, see the following topic in SQL Server Books Online:\n<div class=\"indent\"><a href=\"http://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/library/ms143241.aspx\" id=\"kb-link-47\" target=\"_self\">Using Multiple Versions of SQL Server in a Replication Topology</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"faq-section\" faq-section=\"\">\n<div class=\"faq-panel\">\n<div class=\"faq-panel-heading\" faq-panel-heading=\"\"><span class=\"link-expand-image\"><span class=\"faq-chevron win-icon win-icon-ChevronUpSmall\"></span></span><span class=\"bold btn-link link-expand-text\"><span class=\"bold btn-link\">Full-text search</span></span></div>\n\n<div class=\"faq-panel-body\" faq-panel-body=\"\">\n<div class=\"kb-collapsible kb-collapsible-collapsed\">Full-text search components include the following:<br>\n&nbsp;\n<ul class=\"sbody-free_list\">\n\t<li>Sqlserver.exe</li>\n\t<li>Sql_fulltext_keyfile.dll</li>\n\t<li>Iftsph.dll</li>\n\t<li>Fd.dll</li>\n\t<li>Fdhost.exe</li>\n\t<li>Fdlauncher.exe</li>\n</ul>\nExcept for Sqlservr.exe, these components may not be updated with each cumulative update or service pack for the respective SQL Server product. The versions of these files will change only when there is a fix to the respective component. Generally, you can check the file version of each of these .dll files. The highest version in the list is the version of the full-text search component that is installed on the system.<br>\n<br>\nYou can use one of the following methods to determine the version of the full-text search component that is installed on your system.<br>\n<br>\n<strong>Note</strong> Each of these methods may indicate that the version of the full-text search compnent is either RTM or a version that is earlier than the current version of the database component. We acknowledge that this is a problem and are working on fixing it in a future update.<br>\n<br>\n<strong>Method 1:</strong> Check the version of SQL Server Full-Text Key (Sql_fulltext_keyfile.dll) in the SQL Server 2008 R2 or SQL Server 2008 installation folder. Typically, for SQL Server 2008 R2, this file is located in the following folder:\n\n<div class=\"indent\">%ProgramFiles%\\Microsoft SQL Server\\MSQL10_50.&lt;Instance Name&gt;\\MSSQL</div>\n<br>\nFor SQL Server 2008, this file typically is located in the following folder:\n<div class=\"indent\">%ProgramFiles%\\Microsoft SQL Server\\MSQL10.&lt;Instance Name&gt;\\MSSQL</div>\n<br>\n<strong>Method 2:</strong> Check the following registry subkey:\n\n<div class=\"indent\"><strong class=\"sbody-strong\">HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\\Software\\Microsoft\\Microsoft sql server\\Mssql10_50.instname\\Setup\\SQL_FULLTEXT_ADV</strong></div>\nAn example entry at this registry subkey is the following:<br>\n&nbsp;\n<pre class=\"sbody-pre\">\n\nfeaturelist:  SQL_FullText_Adv=3 SQL_FullText_CNI=3\n\nProductCode:  {9DFA5914-C275-42E0-810E-C88E46A7F9EA}\n\nPatchlevel:   10.50.1765.0\n\nVersion:      10.50.1600.1 </pre>\n<br>\nIn this example entry, the third line (Patchlevel) indicates the current build of full-text search component that is installed, and the fourth line (Version) usually shows the original version of full-text search that is installed. In this case, it is SQL Server 2008 R2.<br>\n<br>\n<strong>Method 3:</strong> Use the Summary.txt file that is created during setup. For SQL Server 2008 R2, this file is located in the following folder:\n\n<div class=\"indent\">%ProgramFiles%\\Microsoft SQL Server\\110\\Setup Bootstrap\\LOG\\Summary.txt</div>\n<br>\nFor SQL Server 2008, this file is located in the following folder:\n<div class=\"indent\">%ProgramFiles%\\Microsoft SQL Server\\100\\Setup Bootstrap\\LOG\\Summary.txt</div>\nSee the following article in the Microsoft Knowledge Base for a known issue that uses full-text search components in SQL Server 2008 installations:\n\n<div class=\"indent\"><a href=\"/en-us/help/973888\" id=\"kb-link-50\" target=\"_self\">973888</a> The Full-Text Search component is not completely rolled back to the Service Pack 1 version after you uninstall Cumulative Update 3 for SQL Server 2008 Service Pack 1 that is applied by using a slipstream installation</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"faq-section\" faq-section=\"\">\n<div class=\"faq-panel\">\n<div class=\"faq-panel-heading\" faq-panel-heading=\"\"><span class=\"link-expand-image\"><span class=\"faq-chevron win-icon win-icon-ChevronUpSmall\"></span></span><span class=\"bold btn-link link-expand-text\"><span class=\"bold btn-link\">SQL Server Master Data Services (MDS)</span></span></div>\n\n<div class=\"faq-panel-body\" faq-panel-body=\"\">\n<div class=\"kb-collapsible kb-collapsible-collapsed\">The MDS Configuration Manager does not show the currently installed version number directly.<br>\n<br>\nBe aware that MDS has a unique versioning scenario in which the SQL Server database engine installation does not necessarily match the MDS version. The version may vary when you compare the SQL Server installation to the binaries deployed in the MDS website and the MDS catalog schema version. Manual steps that use the MDS Configuration Manager tool are required to update and to upgrade the MDS websites and database schemas. You can refer to the following blog post on hotfix and service pack update methodology for MDS:\n<div class=\"indent\"><a href=\"http://sqlblog.com/blogs/mds_team/archive/2010/08/25/downloading-and-installing-sql-server-2008-r2-master-data-services-mds-cumulative-updates.aspx\" id=\"kb-link-51\" target=\"_self\">Downloading and Installing SQL Server 2008 R2 Master Data Services (MDS) Cumulative Updates</a></div>\n<br>\nThe following registry subkey shows the binary versions that are installed on the SQL Server. However, this version does not necessarily match the website and database schema version until the MDS upgrade process is complete.\n<div class=\"indent\"><strong class=\"sbody-strong\">HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\\SOFTWARE\\Microsoft\\Microsoft SQL Server\\Master Data Services 10.5\\CurrentVersion</strong></div>\n<br>\nYou can check the installed product version and schema version by using the following query in the MDS catalog:\n<div class=\"indent\"><span class=\"text-base\"></span>\n\n<pre class=\"sbody-pre\">\n\nselect * from mds.mdm.tblSystem </pre>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"faq-section\" faq-section=\"\">\n<div class=\"faq-panel\">\n<div class=\"faq-panel-heading\" faq-panel-heading=\"\"><span class=\"link-expand-image\"><span class=\"faq-chevron win-icon win-icon-ChevronUpSmall\"></span></span><span class=\"bold btn-link link-expand-text\"><span class=\"bold btn-link\">SQL Server Native Client</span></span></div>\n\n<div class=\"faq-panel-body\" faq-panel-body=\"\">\n<div class=\"kb-collapsible kb-collapsible-collapsed\"><strong>Note&nbsp;</strong>The major SQL Server version of latest SQL Server Native Client is SQL Server 2012. It&rsquo;s compatible with SQL Server 2014.<br>\n<br>\nTo determine the version of SQL Server Native Client, use one of the following methods:<br>\n<br>\n<strong>Method 1:</strong> On the system where you want to find the version of Native Client, start the ODBC Administrator (odbcad32.exe), and then check the <strong class=\"uiterm\">Version </strong>column under the <strong class=\"uiterm\">Drivers </strong>tab.<br>\n<br>\n<strong>Method 2:</strong> Check the following PatchLevel or Version keys at the following registry locations.<br>\n&nbsp;\n<div class=\"table-responsive\">\n<table class=\"table\">\n\t<tbody>\n\t\t<tr class=\"sbody-tr\">\n\t\t\t<th class=\"sbody-th\">SQL version /<br>\n\t\t\tSQL Server Native Client version</th>\n\t\t\t<th class=\"sbody-th\">Registry subkeys</th>\n\t\t</tr>\n\t\t<tr class=\"sbody-tr\">\n\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\">SQL Server 2008 R2</td>\n\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\">HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\\SOFTWARE\\Microsoft\\Microsoft SQL Server\\SQLNCLI10\\CurrentVersion</td>\n\t\t</tr>\n\t\t<tr class=\"sbody-tr\">\n\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\">SQL Server 2008 /<br>\n\t\t\tSQL Server Native Client 10</td>\n\t\t\t<td class=\"sbody-td\">HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\\SOFTWARE\\Microsoft\\Microsoft SQL Server\\SQLNCLI10\\CurrentVersion</td>\n\t\t</tr>\n\t\t<tr Server\\SQLNCLI11\\CurrentVersion</td>\n\t\t</tr>\n\t</tbody>\n</table>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"faq-section\" faq-section=\"\">\n<div class=\"faq-panel\">\n<div kb-collapsible-collapsed\">The browser version should match the highest version of the SQL Server Database Engine and of the instances of Analysis Services that are installed on the computer.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"faq-section\" faq-section=\"\">\n<div class=\"faq-panel\">\n<div class=\"faq-panel-heading\" faq-panel-heading=\"\"><span class=\"link-expand-image\"><span class=\"faq-chevron win-icon win-icon-ChevronUpSmall\"></span></span><span class=\"bold btn-link link-expand-text\"><span class=\"bold btn-link\">Frequently asked questions</span></span></div>\n\n<div class=\"faq-panel-body\" faq-panel-body=\"\">\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n\n<div class=\"kb-collapsible kb-collapsible-collapsed\"><strong>Q1: How do you determine the version of SQL Server when SQL Server is not running?</strong><span class=\"text-base\"></span><br>\n<br>\n<strong>A1:</strong> You can determine the version of SQL Server by using either Method 2 or Method 5 (for SQL Server 2008 or later versions) in the &quot;<a data-content-id=\"\" data-content-type=\"\" href=\"https://support.microsoft.com/help/321185/#howtodetermine\" managed-link=\"\" target=\"\">How to determine which version and edition of SQL Server Database Engine is running</a>&quot; section of this article.<br>\n<br>\n<strong>Q2: How do I map the product versions to product names?</strong><br>\n<br>\n<strong>A2:</strong> You can use the following table as a reference.<br>\n&nbsp;\n<div class=\"table-responsive\">\n<table class=\"table\">\n\t<tbody>\n\t\t<tr class=\"faq-section\" faq-section=\"\">\n<div class=\"faq-panel\">\n<div class=\"faq-panel-heading\" faq-panel-heading=\"\"><span class=\"link-expand-image\"><span class=\"faq-chevron win-icon win-icon-ChevronUpSmall\"></span></span><span class=\"bold btn-link link-expand-text\"><span class=\"bold btn-link\">Frequently used terms and acronyms</span></span></div>\n\n<div class=\"faq-panel-body\" faq-panel-body=\"\">\n<p><span class=\"text-base\"></span><br>\n<span><strong>Cumulative update (CU):</strong> A roll-up update that contains all previous critical on-demand hotfixes to date. Additionally, a CU contains fixes for issues that meet the hotfix acceptance criteria. These criteria may include the availability of a workaround, the effect on the customer, the reproducibility of the problem, the complexity of the code that must be changed, and other topics.</span><br>\n<br>\n<span><strong>Hotfix:</strong></span>A single, cumulative package that includes one or more files that are used to address a problem in a product and are cumulative at the binary and file level. A hotfix addresses a specific customer situation and may not be distributed outside the customer&#39;s organization.<br>\n<br>\n<strong>RTM:</strong> Usually means &quot;release to manufacturing.&quot; In the context of a product such as SQL Server, it indicates that no service packs or hotfixes were applied to the product.<br>\n<br>\n<strong>RTW:</strong> Usually means &quot;release to web.&quot; It indicates a package that was released to the web and made available to customers for downloading.<br>\n<br>\n<strong>Service pack:</strong> A tested, cumulative set of all hotfixes, security updates, critical updates, and updates. Service packs may also contain additional fixes for problems that are found internally since the release of the product and a limited number of customer-requested design changes or features.<br>\n&nbsp;</p>\n\n<p>For more information, go to the following websites:</p>\n\n<ul class=\"sbody-free_list\">\n\t<li><a href=\"/default.aspx?scid=kb;en-us;822499\" id=\"kb-link-58\" target=\"_self\">822499</a> Naming schema for Microsoft SQL Server software update packages</li>\n\t<li><a href=\"/default.aspx?scid=kb;en-us;824684\" id=\"kb-link-59\" target=\"_self\">824684</a>&nbsp;Description of the standard terminology that is used to describe Microsoft software updates</li>\n\t<li><a href=\"/default.aspx?scid=kb;en-us;935897\" id=\"kb-link-60\" target=\"_self\">935897</a> An Incremental Servicing Model is available from the SQL Server team to deliver hotfixes for reported problems</li>\n\t<li><a href=\"http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/software_release_life_cycle\" id=\"kb-link-61\" target=\"_self\">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_release_life_cycle</a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n\n<p><a class=\"bookmark\" id=\"completeversion\"></a></p>\n\n<div><span
